33. To Lingappa Savalgi at Pune, June 7, 1911.

      When    you   have   been   repeatedly    told   orally   and
through letters that you should pay your attention to what
saint Tukarama has told,      namely that      you should   medi-
tate on the Name of God and be devoted to your studies
also, it is surprising how you write as if you have been
told to attend to one thing only and not the other. Anyway,
from now at least study hard, and meditate on the divine
Name with one-pointed devotion.        That will       remove all
your anxiety and doubt,


34.   To a learned Shastri, August 30, 1911.

      Very glad to read the contents of your postcard. Your
writing of books is really an evidence of your great learn-
ing and of your      yogic practice.   But afterall there is a
great difference between verbal knowledge which consists
of words and sentences and experiential knowledge which
does not require the support of what is written in the books
of the learned persons. What I expect of you is that in the
coming month of Sravana you should, completely devote
yourself to meditation on the Name of God. For, as you
very well know to remember the Name of God constitutes
the knowledge of Brahman, whereas not to do so consti-
tutes what is false and illusory.

35. To Sayyadalli alias Kabir of Chimmad, April 7, 1912.

    Very happy to read your letter and to know that a son
is born in your family. You may, if you like, call the son
by the name Khudasahib; and in addition may call him
by any name as your people might wish.

36. To Somanathpant Joshi, February 9, 1913.

      Exceedingly pleased to read the poems you have com-
posed,    Others also liked them very much.       All the same,
the joy one derives from them springs up only when the
composition is read and understood. On the other hand the
             Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi              69

joy which is derived by meditating constantly and regularly
on the Name of God and the consequent contemplation or
the direct realization of God can never be described by
words. It has simply to be experienced, for it cannot be
communicated to others by means of words. So what is
chiefly expected of you, in accordance with the teaching of
St. Ramadasa in his Dasabodha       (4.3.10-12) is that you
would also devote your time to an intense concentrated
meditation on the Name of God, which is imparted to you
by your spiritual teacher.

    There is a lot of difference between Jnana and Jneya,
ie. between knowledge and the object of knowledge. Any
description of knowledge will fall short of the condition of
the realization of that knowledge; for, in that condition
of identity there is no distinction between the knower and
the known. Along with      the ignorance    of the objects of
knownledge, vanishes also the awareness of oneself being
the knower of that knowledge. What remains is the object
of knowledge namely, God Himself.

37.   To Ramchandra Dada Ranade, February 12, 1913.

      It is good that you write to me not simply on certain
occasions only.   I am highly pleased to see this.   I could
not however send you any     reply because there was none
available to me to whom I eould have instructed to write.
Please do write as often as you can and give the pleasure
 of knowing everything about the well-being and health
of your mother, sister, and yourself.      As you know very
well to remember God       is to participate in  His nature
whereas to forget Him is to fall into the illusory samsara.
1 have therefore to tell you and to all who are your rela-
 tives and friends that they should devote their maximum
 time and energy to the meditation on the Name of God
 with fixity of attention and faith.

     Herewith I have enclosed a copy of the poems which
 the young man, Somanath Panchanadikar has composed for
70       Prof. 2२. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


your perusal. I have written to him saying that that much
time he could have usefully spent in meditation, though it
is also true that his poems would be useful in moulding his
own intellect and understanding.

       Lingappa Savalagi has gone to Inchgiri. I shall inform
you the date by which I shall be going over to Solapur.

38.    To Haripant Limaye, Bombay, September 6, 1913.

       God will be helpful to you according to your faith in
Him. All your desires will be fulfilled without any effort
provided you do the meditation         on the Name of God im-
parted to you by your spiritual Teacher, with all your
concentration and faith.      To remember God always is to
make room for joy forever.

39.    To his eldest son, October 6, 1913.

       Behave   in a way that will indicate     your devotion.
straight-forwardness, and desirelessness.     You will then be
fortunate to hear such words as will bring fragrance to
you.


40.    To his son Krishnajipant who was serving in the office
       of the Mamlatdar at Jath,

       Devote your time in doing meditation without wast-
ing a single moment in useless talk with such friends as
have no work on hand. While dealing with your superior
officers however, you shall have to spend some time as it
is necessary and forms a part of your duty which you must
do, Do not entertain any suspicions or talk about it unless
you have reason to do so. Nor should you seek to expose
the weak points of your inferiors.

       Speak sweet and pleasing words to all, though inter-
nally you should be cautious.      Do not accept any bribe on
any account for, it shall have to be returned some time in
the future.     Wealth and woman belonging to others must
be ruthlessly kept      away at all costs,   even though they
             Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi              71

might be within your easy      reach. Even the     innermost
greedy and lustful ideas about these will be immediately
known by a real saint. Be therefore alert at all times for,
one does not know when he might be in deep water.

    Hence it is very necessary that you should resort to
the only meritorious way, namely of meditation on the
Name of God and of having a fixed gaze on His vision which
you might have before your eyes. Remember the Name at
all times and in all your activities, and be ever looking
at the form of God. This is the only means by which you
can shield yourself against any temptation in life.

41. To Ramachandrapant Kulkarni of Horti.

      It is now the tenth or twelfth day since we all have
come to Jamkhandi. It is really difficult to describe how by
the grace of God, devotion is gathering momentum day by
day. God fulfills the desires of his devotees, whether they
arise in them on account of their sense of duty or due to
their longings for pleasures and material gains.    But this
ought to teach them that they ought to remain contented
with whatever is given by God.     This is not however pos-
sible unless man leaves the point of view of his selfish ego,
and remembers God at all times.      Either his desires will
then be satisfied, or he shall be contented with the condi-
tion in which he would find himself.

42.   To his youngest son.

   It is now well-known that the Rohilas      are creating
more and more trouble in the Karajagi district of the state
of Jath.   What however we must do is to go by the only
way of practising our duty    (Dharma) namely, of meditat-
ing on the divine Name with absolute faith in God. Then,
success will be on our side, and there will be an end to all
the troubles.   That is why you should see,   as I have told
you personally, that there would be no exception
                                                 to your
Practice of meditation.   Do not sleep during   daytime and
72      Prof. R. ७. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


utilize your time in doing your studies and in the house-
hold duties.

43.   It is not clear to whom this letter is addressed.

      When I retrospect I feel now-a-days that there: has
been a change in my nature for the better. One-fourth of
my cravings and evil tendencies have been on the decrease,
yet I feel I have the fear in my mind that this may be a
temporary phase      only   and that I    might    revert to   my
original nature.   But how wonderful it is that I remember
at the same time what I had heard very often            from my
spiritual teacher, that we should never allow our intellect
to be clouded by such pessimistic thoughts, lest, notwith-
standing the grace of God, we should be blind to the Guru’s
words of advice and fail to see the         divine light which
comes out of devout meditation on the Name of God, just
as the King Dhrtarastra (who was blind both physically
and spiritually)   did not like the advice given to him by
Vidura who was morally and spiritually great.

44.   To Parvatibai Gokhale of Jamkhandi.

      Where   our heart     shall be   depends    upon what    we
bring into practice daily. Either the affairs of the worldly
life or the discipline and the experiences of the spiritual
life would be felt as the dearest and the closest to our heart.
This has been found to be true since the ancient times.
There were atheists even at the times of Valmiki, the
author of the Ramayana. The same happened at the time of
the great battle of the Mahabharata. The Kauravas did not
believe even in the words of Krsna. The enemies of Tuka-
rama hated him for composing spiritual poems. Natural it is
that the owls should hate the Sun, that the robbers should
be angry with the moon-light; the misers should dislike
the donors of wealth, or that an iconoclast who has no eye
for beauty should break idols of worship. Even so, one who
is immersed in samsara will necessarily form the habit of
             Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi              73

getting himself interested more and more in transitory
pleasures only.

     Therefore what ought to be done by a spiritually
minded person, is that he should form the habit of medi-
tating daily and regularly with an ever-increasing faith and
love. How will such a man waste all his nights in sleep
only? He will devote the minimum of his time in sleep, and
spend all the remaining time     in the silent meditation on
the Name of God.

45. To Shankarrao Kumathekar, Venkatrao Mestri, Datto-
      pant Phadke, and other disciples of Solapur.

     Please remember that meditation for one hour with
faith and joy in the morning as well as in the evening
without any exception removes the dullness of the mind
the tendency to fall into sleep as also all   other undesira-
ble effects and impressions of other activities   during day
and night.   If this practice is carried on for a long time,
there will spring up in the heart a real love and friend-
ship with God. What this means is, in other words, that
God will manifest in some form or the other before the
devotee who would then along        with the meditation on
the Name fix his gaze on that very vision to such   an extent
that not only sleep and idleness, but interest in all other
Godless objects will automatically fade away.


46.   Written as a general letter and probably sent to
      Amburao

    One can understand how a person might suffer from
anxiety due to the dearth of commodities which are essen-
tial for   maintaining one’s livelihood. But on     that very
account, it might be    possible for him to    remember the
Name of God sometimes at least.       As time passes, what
generally happens however is that anxieties increase and
man feels the necessity of acquiring more and more moriey
and thereby make his wordly existence more happy,
                                                  tom-
74     Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


fortable and secure. This makes him more and more greedy
but at the same time, more and more negligent of his duty.
towards God, which he had once accepted with the hope
that it would be a means of solving his mundane problems.,
Perhaps, he might have suffered from some sudden diffi-
culties which might have cropped up even while he was
doing his regular meditational exercise. Whatever may be
the reason for the setback, such a man devotes then all his
time 10 make his worldly life a success.       All   his senses,
especially his     tongue, eyes, and ears become engaged in
acquiring the pleasures of life, and in doing so he does not
mind even if he commits a number of sins.

     Instead    of this, if he   were to engage his senses in
attending to his daily meditation on the divine Name with
faith and devotion and feel in his heart of hearts that this
alone constitutes his chief duty, he would come to know
gradually that all his difficulties are over by the grace of
God, and that whatever would fall to his lot either in his
worldly or spiritual life happens by the will of God. He
would become convinced that all his sins are washed away,
that all the merits of good deeds (punya) are accumulated
in him, that all his anxieties are over, and that his     mind
and body are perfectly sound and healthy. Of course, this
would result when his meditational devotion would make
him see God face to face, and not otherwise.

     What one must therefore        do is to begin to meditate
on the Name of God and repent for having wasted his time
till then. When his constant, regular and daily meditation
for a long time would amount to a great heap as if, God
will manifest before    him. And then, he would experience
the real disgust (Vairagya) for all the Godless objects in
the world.     Then alone will his devotion be absorbing, un-
swerving, joyful and as springing up from the bottom of
his heart.   He will then be a witness of all that passes.in
his mind as well as in those of others.      This is the real
Jnana-marga, the path of knowledge.
             Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi                  95

47, To his eldest son.
      What I wish of you is that you should never forget
the Name of God. Not only should you meditate with a
concentrated mind and absolute faith daily and regularly
at fixed hours, but you should also remember God through-
out all your activities, whether you are sitting, walking,
lying down, eating or are busy in doing any other work.
Besides, you must be honest and straight-forward in all
your dealings. For, upon this only will depend your pros-
perity. In short, being my son you should so behave as will
be befitting to my reputation.

48.

What can the Guru        do to him, who does not control his
mind? How can one aspire to be the prince             among the
devotees, if he continues to be a slave of the senses and
seeks only the pleasures of life? He might only pretend
to be a devotee of God, so long as his devotion is useful
to him as a means to fulfil his     desires. But he does    not
understand    that he is thereby drifted more and more to
the enjoyments of sensuous pleasures and other gains in
life. His devotion becomes only a cloak for concealing his
attachment to the objects of his desires. What is therefore
of primary importance from the spiritual point of view is
that one should first possess a full control over his senses
and mind in order that his devotion to God may turn out
to be genuine.

         81.   To Jivabalappa Sangam.

               Make your heart absolutely pure, and your mind per-
         fectly unperturbed and steady. And with full faith in your
         Guru, meditate daily on the divine Name imparted to you
         by him with unswerving devotion. And during the remain-
         ing hours of the day and night also remember the Name
         as often as you can. This is my advice to you.


         52.

          Do not suppose, as people in general wrongly do, that
     thinking about spiritual knowledge is a vain pursuit. Do
     think about it as and when you get time and do so seriously
     and not as a pastime. Man becomes proud and blind as if
     by greed and arrogance when he gets even a little rise in
     status and social position. One can see the effect of this
     even in the spiritual domain when such a man begins to
     meditate or is fortunate to get some spiritual experience.
     But remember that his pride alone would ruin him com-
     pletely, materially as well as spiritually. None will be
     available then to open his eyes to the truth. That is why
     I am awakening you out of your ignorance, even at the
     beginning of your spiritual career.

53. To Dada Pandit Anna.

    The two paths of activity and non-activity run counter
to each other, but the two together indicate all the duals
such as knowledge and ignorance, censure and praise, love
and hatred, description and direct experience, attachment
and non-attachment and so on. The way of activity or
Pravrtti which quickly generates the egoistic attachment
 to the traditional and credulous way of thinking and believ-
ing becomes so thoroughly ingrained in the mind of man
that it becomes difficult to eradicate it altogether. It leads
a man to believe that what is destined to happen will never
fail to happen and that even gods in heaven or the incarna-
tions of God cannot avoid what the Fate has alloted to
them. Such a hardened belief makes them stick up to their
bodily and mental pleasures and pains and to their greed
and other emotions, such as love and hate, so much so that
they never get any occasion to become aware of the fact
that all   these   things   are   ultimately   perishable.   Their
notions, about honour and dishonour, merit           and demerit
(papa and punya), duty, charity, and about the nature of
God and methods of worship and meditation are all steep-
ed in utter ignorance.

    Naturally, their whole life is wasted either in hot pur-
suit of the perishable pleasures in life and of the means
to attain them, or in idleness, anxieties, slothfulness or
hatred of others. And, if one life is not sufficient to achieve
what they want, the law of karma will give them always
new and newer lives to allow them finish their incomplete
works. In short, they will always be mounfed on the wheel
of Maya from which there would be no escape.            Not only
do they not have any idea of what exists beyond the affairs
of samsara, they do not also understand as to what con-
stitutes the real source of happiness in their mundane life.
To them, selfishness alone at all costs is the be-all and end-
all of life.   If that is secure, they would not mind giving
misery and pain to others.        The altruistic ideal of giving
78       Prof. R. 9. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage

happiness and joy to others at the cost of one’s own happi-
ness and joy is unknown and ununderstandable to them.
               3




     As opposed to this the Nivrtti marga that is, the medi-
tative and contemplative way of life,          which erroneously
appears ‘to the untutored mind as the path of inactivity
and-slothfulness, has its starting-point in the self-surren-
der at the feet of the spiritual teacher and the consequent
earnest’ desire’to be in the ‘company-of the good and- the
holy.    In course of time, as the practice of meditation on
the Name of God and contemplation on His form becomes
rooted deep in the body and mind, there remains no cause
for being greedy     or ruffled, whatever may be the course
of destiny. No real devotee of God will then complain of
his stars being against him, or say in despair that he must
suffer in accordance with what lies in store for him by
the law of destiny. For, God being omnipotent, can change
the otherwise unavoidable lines of his destiny.             All this
however is not possible for those who live like frogs in
their own self-circumscribed well of ignorance. Let-them
perform     thousands   of   sacrifices   during   their   life-time,
or do the penance by standing on a toe.            Yet, so long as
they do not understand that the ‘Summum Bonum’ of life
consists in going in the direction opposite to the current of
samsara, like a fish swimming upstream against the force
of water, ie., so long as they do not realize that the highest
duty of man is to see one’s own immaculate form and to
become one with it, anything done will be of no permanent
value.


     One must therefore give his best thought to under-
stand this all. For, without intelligent inquiry, none will
be able to find out the Truth. As no amount of discursive
intellect will be of any avail one must surrender himself
to a great spiritual teacher who is capable of opening the
eves of others to the Truth, and adopt his understanding,
his way of search, and his insight into the nature of Reality.
            Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi               79

54. To Shiraningappa Chikkona and Nandyappa Anna.

    If there is some malady and if it is to be removed, the
physician must be honest and the patient must have faith
in the physician, As soon as you get up from your.bed.early

grace of Géd, meditate on the divine Name. Do this
in the afternoon and before going to-bed as well. Along
with this eat in the morning and in the evening for eleven
days, fried flour of Moonga mixed with two ounces of jag-
gery and two ounces of good ghee. Yet, between the two,
what is of utmost importance is that you should meditate
intensely, regularly and daily three times a day.    +    - ”

59, To Narahararao Pleader Vijapur,’ February 12, 1905.

    Your kind letter for me addressed to Amburao Maha-
raja was read by me with great pleasure. So,-I -feel-like
writing to you the following. The spiritual or the illumina-
tional kirid of knowledge is like fire which burns all the
blemishes as soon as it is lit in the-heart. As-a result of
this, everything which
                     is capable of being burnt becomes
an object of displéasure and disgust. This"is known as
Virakti, a condition which is most favourable for enhancing
the intensity of devotion to God. But where there is no
spark, there cannot be any illumination, nor will there’ be
any Virakti, nor real    devotion. There    will only be the
bodily egoism, which is the enemy of spiritual knowledge.

    Surrender therefore one should at the feet of-the Guru
and meditate upon ‘the divine’    Name imparted by ‘him.
With his one-pointed    gaze, and by the power of his medi-
tation, he will be able to visualize the’ forms of God. Then,
it should always be his duty to see that all these three
namely, Vairagya, bhakti and Jnana ase always present.
As a further precaution. he should keep himself always in
the company of those good souls in whose hearts both
the Name and Forms       of God are    permanently fixed, -
80     Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


     What I wish to write today is about the six so-called
enemies of the spiritual life.   Of course, the common belief
that they are enemies is true on the level of morality only.
But on this account it need not     be said that these natural
tendencies of the mind are mere enemies.         These can. be
treated as friends or allies also if one is able to utilize the
power which they possess. For instance, though Kama (de-
sire) might act as an enemy if it is directed to win the love
of a woman other than his wife, it will act as a great
friend if it is directed towards cultivating the devotion for
God. Instead of being angry with the saints, one should
be angry with his own wayward and uncontrollable senses.
Do not increase your greed for body and all that you pos-
sess, but increase it you must in having more and more
grace of God and of the Guru by serving them in all ways.
Too much attachment is bad if it is concentrated on your
family members only, but it      is excellent if it is with the
good and the holy. Why should one-be arrogant to friends?
He should be so to the wicked. And, finally, what will you
gain by being jealous of other persons. Rather be jealous
of the hold that the samsara or Maya has upon you.

     This is how one can transform his evil nature into good
one, selfishness into altruism. and thereby help himself be-
come fit to receive spiritual knowledge from the Guru.
Saint Tukarama remembered only the latter portion of
his name, ‘Rama’, and ultimately became equal to or one
with ‘Rama’. His sense of being a separate individuality
became completely drowned in his being aware that what
exists for ever is the Atman (Atmarama). In other words,
if what is capable of being measured is equated with what
cannot be measured then what emerges is not the person-
ality of Tukarama, but the Impersonality of Rama, which
eternally transcends the Personal aspect of God in spite of
its being immanent in it. Saint Tukarama can be said from
this point of view, as being both Personal and the Im-
personal aspects of God. So long as he was living he re-
presented the Personal aspect, though he was at the same
               Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi                        81

time experiencing the Impersonal God. But after his death,
he became one with the Impersonal. Even then the Imper-
sonal has the power to manifest itself on occasions as the
Personal in the form of Tukarama though not in flesh and
body. This will explain how finite vision of God as small
as a sesame seed is pregnant with the Infinite visions of
Him.


56. To Narkararao, Pleader, Vijapur, May 4, 1905.

    Your kind letter has remained unreplied for a long
time. You have raised in it a problem as to how it can be
maintained’ that God who is fully immanent in all the mov-
able and immovable objects of the world, is residing in a
house which he has built for himself as if away from this
universe, and which is as small as a sesame seed.
  a




     This is really a problem which will bewilder the intel-
lect, But as given below there are several other problems
which will equally bewilder the intellect or offend the
Logical ‘law of contradiction’ which states that two con-
tradictory propositions cannot be true at the same time.
(1)   Saint Ramadasa says about God that              there is not a
single portion of space in which God does‘not exist.               But
there is   another weighty sentence from the                Bhagavata
which   says   about   God,   that   neither   does    he    dwell    in
Vaikuntha, nor in the disc of Sun, nor in the hearts of              the
yogins, but in the midst of his devotees who sing in praise
the glorious deeds of God. (2) The demon Hiranyakasyapu
had obtained a boon from God that neither during day nor
during night will he be killed by either a man or any
beast. And yet he was killed. (3) In the sacred book
known as ‘Gurucaritra’, it is narrated how a learned
Brahmin    was   shorn   off of his pride          when     the   saint
Nrsinhasarasvati    caused    an     untouchable
                                          to repeat the
Vedic hymns,   Even so, the saint Jnanesvara is credited
with the miracle of havirig made a buffalo speak out the
Vedic hymns, and to cause a wall to walk some distance.
8        Prof. R. 9. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


It is for you to think if this probably means that the grace
of the    Guru is competent to make a person as dull as a
buffalo to recite the Vedas and a person who is as stupid
and slothful as a stone-wall to become conscious and intel-
ligent and walk towards the path of God after leaving 08-
hind him all the three sinful thoughts and deeds, namely
greed for other men’s wealth and land, and a lustful eye on
a woman not his own.      (4) The great yogi, Cangadeva, is said
to have lived for fourteen hundred years and that he used
to ride on a tiger. What can be the implication of this ex-
cept perhaps that’ the yogin could live for such a long
time, because he could have tasted throughout his life       the
elixir on his tongue on account of meditation on the Name
of God, and that he must have brought under control the
tiger in the form of desires, anger, greed, infatuation, pre-
tension and jealousy.     (5) Will it be possible for any human
being to read all the enormous number of Tukarama’s ab-
hangas namely over four Koti (ten million) and’ laksa
(hundred thousand) in his life time? Are they available
at all? Leaving then the literal meaning of the words, we
must understand the implications of them.           Then ‘Chara-
koti’ (koti meaning condition) will mean during all the
conditions or hours of life; four conditions of life being
wakefulness, sleep, dream and supramental condition and
four periods consisting of morning, afternoon, twilight and
night.   One ‘Laksa’    (laksa,   meaning target)   would   mean
one object only’,      that is, God who is to be contemplated
upon.     (6)   Similarly we are told that the trees which .
had become life-less   began fo           have foliage again
when the sage ‘Valmiki’ did his           penance there, Does
this not mean that by trees which had become life-less, we
are to understand men who lived in that ‘forest and who
were thoroughly ignorant of Atmajnana, Self-realization
began to know what it means by the grace of the Guru
(7) Saint Tukarama also along with all other great saints
holds the view that one who’ realizes how the self is noth-
ing but the Brahman,        has no rebirth.   And yet he says
                   Sri Bhausachib Maharaja uf Umadi               83

  to God that he would not mind being born again provided
ˆ he is assured of having the company of the good and the
  holy. Here also, what does rebirth mean? Does it mean,
  coming into the womb of the mother or transformation of
    the jiva into the Brahman? Unless we have two meanings
    of ‘rebirth’    (Garbha-womb and Vasa-dwelling) we shall
    not be able to resolve the contradiction.    (8) The same diffi-
    culty will be there in understanding how the Lord, could
    become infinite Visvarupa and how again at the request of
`   Arjuna could transform himself into the finite form of
    Krsna with four hands.


        In.all the above and similar cases, we should take the
    precaution of not being led away by the literal meanings
    of words, but rather be guided by the implications which
    they contain.    Considered from this point of view, as well
    as from the view-point of the nature of spiritual Reality,
    it would be correct to hold that it has got the capacity of
    manifesting itself in forms which are at once. infinitesimal
    and.infinite, or as is often said, presenting itself as smaller
    than the smallest and    larger than the largest. Verily, who
    can prevent it from becoming the infinite out of its sesame-
    like small form, or from becoming the Visvarupa out of the
    finite form with four arms or vice-versa? And who is there
    to challenge the experience of a saint who would tell us
    that this is just the description of the experience?        One
    who doubts this should go by the way of his spiritual
    teacher, win his grace and see for himself the truth of
    what all this means. One who realizes his       own ‘immaculate
    form will go beyond      all the verbal     distinctions and the
    superficial meanings of the words.


    57. To Narahararao Pleader, Vijapur, January 25, 1906.

        Your letter to hand. I am exceedingly pleased to note
    that your deep interest in    spiritual life has enabled you
    to spare some time to think seriously about certain pro-
    blems the solution of which    will not only be useful to you
84       Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage

but to all those who seek to know the life divine. In your
letter you    have   drawn my     attention   to   a very funda-
mental point in spiritual experience, namely,          that there
cannot be any visual or tactual contact with the Nirguna
Brahman, much less any conversation with it, if at all
according to the statement of the scriptures, the        Nirguna
Brahman is the only one Reality. It should cause no sur-
prise to anyone that you are taking so much trouble to
know the truth of the matter, since even saint Ekanath
burnt his midnight oil to find out a mistake of a penny in
the accounts of his master which he had maintained, and
even the sage Sukacarya had to toil very hard in rooting
out his egoism before he could meet his Guru and know
from him the pathway to God.

     Verily, what goes beyond speech defies any attempt to
describe it by means of words.       And yet, it is a paradox
of mystical life, that none will understand the nature of
that unspeakable Reality unless somehow it is communi-
cated by the teacher      to the disciple    by means of words.
Should we therefore say on this account that what is in-
describable and unspeakable       is described     and spoken by
words? Can the words be the exact transcription of what
goes beyond the words? What really happens is that the
Reality which is remote is somehow described by means
of analogy, simile and metaphor which after all fall short
of the exact and full transcription of it.

     Even so, when the Nirguna Brahman presents itself or
manifests before the devotee as qualified or Saguna Brah-
man, what occurs is that it is reflected as if in a mirror
and is    said to have   become   immanent in a person.     But
this does not mean that in becoming immanént the Brah-
man has lost its real nature of being transcendent or        in-
dependent of everything else.     Its being    immanent shows
only how the transcendent, qualityless, and formless Brah-
man makes itself amenable to be seen and touched by the
devotee and to holding conversation with him
             Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi                   85


      In fact, it is the saguna nature of Brahman, that is,
the Brahman in its relation to the devotee that makes the
latter convinced in the first place that Brahman is not
something which is altogether alien to him, but that, on the
contrary it is as intimately connected and related to him
as one person can be with another person. In other words,
he is first convinced of the facts that he can see the Brah-
man, touch the’Brahman and hold conversation with him
as if the Brahman is also a finite person, who in turn is
seeing the devotee, touching him and holding conversation
with him, It is from this basic experience of Brahman as
saguna, that is as possessing form, shape, size and various
other qualities of colour, light, sound, and the states of
mind, ete. that he is lifted to discern in the second place,
that notwithstanding these qualities, the Brahman has its
own     independent,    transcendent,   and    infinite   nature,
namely the Nirguna aspect which exists even though it is
not seen or touched by anyone or none         has even held any
conversation with it.




   It was exactly in this manner that the supreme God
is said to’ have .taken births and thus incarnated in        this
mortal world. These incarnations moved and acted amongst
people as if they too were endowed with similar or the
same oualities as the people. But truly speaking, they were

quite different from all of them. In other words, notwith-
standing their saguna nature the incarnations of God are
believed to have retained their Nirguna aspect unimpaired
not only throughout their sojourn on this earth, but also
after their departure from here. The incarnations of Rama
and Krsna, for instance, were just like ordinary peovle
                                                        so
long as they lived on earth, but they are remembered even
today as having both the saguna and Nirguna aspects. Un-
less this is assumed to be correct, what the saints like
Janesvara, Tukarama and Ramadasa, and a host of others
have said, namely that they had not only seen and touched

                                  *
86      Prof. R. 5, Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage

God, put have had also conversed with him, cannot be ac-
cepted as true. Will you now say, as you have written in
your letter, quoting the authority of the scriptures (sruti),
that where there is duality, there is the fear of death?
The    saguna or the personal God of all these saints ought
certainly to have been the cause of fear to them; if the God
whom they had seen or touched or with whom they had
held conversation was      different from   them. But do you
say, that they were afraid of death or of anything else?
If not, will you qualify the statement of the scriptures or
say with the saints themselves that the Personal aspect of
God is neither incompatible with His Impersonal aspect,
107 with the experience of      their union with God?     Once
you grant that the saints themselves had gone beyond the
egoism of their body, mind, senses and intellect, and had
become one with the vision of their own immaculate Self,
would there be any difference still left between the saguna
and the Nirguna aspects of God? Is not the living saint
both saguna and nirguna in the very same instant? Look-
ing at the fact that the saint is living in flesh and blood as
well as the fact that God is immanent in him, he becomes
an illustration of the Saguna aspect of God. Take into con-
sideration, even while he is living, only his experience of
the vision of his immaculate Self, and not of his physical
body, mind etc. and then the same saint will be an illustra-
tion of the Nirguna aspect of God.



      To realize this highest experience of the spiritual life,
one must do the greatest penance of holding fast the Name
of God in his throat and mind throughout every moment
of his life and contemplate incessantly on the vision of his
Self. No sneezing, yawning or coughing will then be an
hindrance to his uttering the Name of God. Corresponding
to the 21600 breaths during 24 hours, there will be an equal
humber of the repetitions of the Name of God.
                Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi                   87

58. To a certain well-known person who thought too much
    about himself and thoughtlessly said that ‘Truth can
    have na success in this world’ probably to Vasudevrao
    Bidnur, February 9, 1900.

    What do the people in general understand by ‘Truth’,
in the first place? It is nothing but the name given fo their
supposed self-importance on account of the egoism which
arises in them due to their short-lived status or position in
society, and to their false belief that the body and all that
is attached to it have lasting value. At best, truth is, as
they define, the sense of duty, which they are called to
perform according to the need of the society in which they
live and their ability to perform it. Even then truth is not
an unmixed virtue for more often than not, it is prompted
by selfish motives.       Even much of the so-called altruism
which is expressed in philanthropic acts            of charity and
well-being of others, is on scrutiny found to be motivated
by selfish ends. Truth, in short, according to the popular
usage is that intellectual belief about something which is
 considered to be infallible on account of its being rooted
in selfishness, self-conceit and disregard to higher interests
and values, except perhaps a sense of duty which is propor-
tionate to the wages it earns, That is why the           concept of
truth becomes relative from man to man and is very often
confused with what is expedient and pragmatic on a parti-
cular occasion only. To quote one instance from the great
 epic, Mahabharata, it is generally believed that Yudhis-
thara who was considered to be the incarnation of Dharma
or Truth retained his reputation of being so in spite of
his having told a white lie,  namely, he did not know
 whether   it   was     Asvathama, the     son of   Dronacarya,   or
‘the elephant known by the same name who was dead, not-
 withstanding his knowledge that it was the latter who was
really dead.


    Similar was the case            with even the great among the
Sages   and     Gods,   such   as    Narada,   Brahmadeva. ‘Indra,
      88     Prof. R. 5. Rantade and His Spiritual Lineage

      Candra, etc. who lied and yet were great. Even Prahlada
      the greatest of the devotees told God that he had nothing
      to offer to him, since   he had   already surrendered every-
      thing that belonged to him, and yet begged of God to for-
      give his father whom he     had affectionately nourished in
      the innermost recesses of his heart. Thus knowingly or un-
      knowingly untruth is concealed deep below a superficial
      layer of truth, which unfortunately passes as truth, even
      though as observed above it is mixed with selfishness and
      cunninghess,


           What then is the real Truth? It is that which cannot
      be eclipsed for ever by untruth or ignorance, though for
      some time, like the Sun whose light becomes dimmed by
      an intervening cloud, it is not clearly discerned on account
      of the several imaginings, egoism, desires and attachment
      to wealth, house, land, progeny, woman ete. Devoid of
      this all, the truth shines by its own lustre. But this will
      be known and experienced, provided one goes by the way
      as pointed out by the spiritual teacher, and meditates re-
      gularly on the Name of God, with faith, love, and deter-
      mination. Who will not respect a man, who has left off
      egoism, hatred, desires and attachment as described above,
      and goes on even while he is doing his duty and other
      activities of the worldly life repeating the divine Name,
      as if he is a faithful dog who barks     for the sake of his
      master against all that is evil, suspicious or dangerous? His
      only concern flies in preserving even after his own death
      the reputation of his Master who is none else but God,
      namely, that he brings protection, peace and joy at the
      doors of His devotees.

          But what a misfortune that people do not wish to go
      to the root of the matter and instead are satisfied by ob-
      serving what is superficial and by accepting blindly what
      comes to them by mere tradition. They believe that the
      Lord Krsna could retain his celibate life in spite of his
      loose behaviour with sixteen thousand Gopis.      In saying


The
             Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi                 89

so have they not sacrificed the great truth that Krsna-hood
or the fact of the realization of Brahman was not even
slightly disturbed, even though Krsna was in the midst
of thousands of temptations of flesh? Considered thus from
the spiritual point of view, that is from the point of view
of the highest truth, should Draupadi be still known as
the wife of the five Pandavas? Will it not be better to
construe this traditional belief as a metaphorical descrip-
 tion of the love for God’s name as being the consort of the
fivefold prana (vital breath) in the human being? Simi-
larly, there is the general notion that one should not try
to trace out the beginning of the spiritual life of a sage;
for it may have its root in a sinful life. But ‘contrary to
this belief, it will he of great spiritual advantage to search
and discover that the origin lies in the divine will.

      In short, truth which in its highest sense is identical
with Reality can never be found without the Realization
of the Atman.    But once it is discovered there will be all
joy, success, and peace.


89.   To Haripant, Antajipant, Vasudevarao Savaikar,
      Ramarao Tarke, Chintopant Apte, and others.

      Your kind letter of 26th December reached me on the
 7th January.

      Before I proceed to write about spiritual matters, let
 me first write about haw a man becomes egoistic without
 being aware of it, inasmuch as his whole attention and
 attachment is on his body, mind and the senses. Let us
 Suppose that a high, reputed official was going by a street
 at midnight and that he was stopped by a guard of the
 city and interrogated as to who he was. But instead of
 giving a full and satisfactory information about himself.
 he became aware of his own high position and answered
 with pride, ‘It is 7. Not being able to understand the im-
 plication of that न" the guard asked him again to state his
 Mame and address upon which the      official had to   shed his
90      Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage

egoism a little and explain to the guard who he was. Now
who was at fault in this case, the guard or the official? Of
course, the official, you would like to say with-me.        For
had he given full information about himself at the outset
he could have retained his dignity with grace and the guard
would have been satisfied without any subsequent feeling
of regret or embarrassment.


     This will explain how very essential it is that one
must drop consciousness that he is body only, and that in
order to achieve this he must be in the company of a realiz-
ed person.    The man is known by the company he keeps.
Even a parrot learns what he is taught by one in whose
company he remains.       No doubt, what     one is essentially
and internally cannot be known by observing him only
externally.   A servant   may   not   know   what   wealth his
master possesses.   Even so, the external dress or behaviour
is not necessarily the index of whether a ‘man is or is not
sannyasin.    One can leave his house and family, and show
by his intellectual knowledge that he        has achieved the
Reality, but in     fact he may   be internally     attached to
samsara, and possess all the desires and emotions of the
mind.                                   न
     In ‘Bhakti-Vijaya’ a story is told about a Brahmin who
used to say to his wife that he would become like the saint
Santoba. Being tired to hear this again and again his wife
asked him to become like Santoba without any loss of
time.   Carried away by the false notion that he was        as
great as Santoba in point of knowledge and dispassion he
approached the latter, but being puffed up with pride and
arrogance he did not even make a courtesy salutation
to him. Knowing that the vanity of the Brahmin had
touched his brain and spoiled his intellect as if by the
drinking of wine, Santoba first deprived him of his clothes
and said to him, ‘now indeed you are like me’. But as the
cold of the night increased the Brahmin began to shiver
and weep. Next day, when he felt greatly hungry, Santoba
             Sri Bhausahib Maharaja of Umadi                  91

gave him a bunch of the bitter leaves of the Neem tree to
eat. The poor Brahmin-began to cry hoarse and curse his
fate. Thereupon Santoba allowed him to go home if he
liked, and said that he would tell his wife not to be cross
with him, but allow him to remain peacefully in the house.
The Brahmin became immensely pleased and_ saluted
Santoba again and again. Thus, the story makes it clear
that man does not generally come to know what he really
is and what his real desires are till the vanity about his
superficial, verbal knowledge is thoroughly washed away.

      A few more examples will clearly point out to you all
how ordinary men become satisfied by knowing the super-
ficial meanings of words, but how the same         words carry
totally different and deeper meanings to those who are
wise and thoughtful. It is generally believed that a great
surprise spread into the     three worlds when it       became
known that Saint Tukarama was weighed against God and
that the balance was exact.        Now, can this literally hap-
pen?    Can the surprise penetrate below the depths of the
earth, or rise high into the heavens?    One might say that
this is only a poetic way of description. But a better mean-
ing is possible if the three worlds are understood as mean-
ing meditation on the divine Name, contemplation on the
vision by means of the eyes, and attention to both medita-
tion and contemplation by means of the mind.         And when
Tukarama could stand these three tests with success, it {€~
came a matter of great surprise to all.     Or, a better mean-
ing still would be to say that Tukarama could go beyond
both the spheres of activity, and non-activity
                                               and beyond
all the limitations (upadhis) of these two, by means
                                                        of
Meditation and contemplation and by keepin
                                               g his  eyes
half-open, so that he could have his gaze on
                                                the Atman,
and    exclude all other things.   One   can as well say that it
was a surprise to all that Tuka
                                rama could have concentra
                                                          t-
ed his attention on the vision of the
                                         Atman in front of him
10 spite of the three great temp
                                 tations of woman, wealth,
and Jand,
92      Prof. ह. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage

    Consider again the three words ‘dhira’, ‘udara’ and
‘gambhira’ which ordinarily mean a person having patience,
courage, and conviction respectively.  Spiritually, however
they have specific meanings, One can be said to be ‘dhira’
who patiently bears all that befalls him with joy and with
the thought that the one doer of all things is God only.
He is courageous    if he can sacrifice everything in the
world for the sake of devotion to God. And, he can exhibit
the deep moral conviction of his mind if like Tukarama, he
can declare that all the women in the world, excepting
his wife, are in the place of his mother,

     Now to the question, who can be said to be a man
of purity?      I would like to answer that he is pure who
sees the presence of God in some form or other before his
very eyes.      One who does his meditation daily, without
being tired and one who repents for having wasted his life
without any devotional attitude to God, can also be said to
be pure of heart.


     As for the direct vision of God, it must be noted that
He is not seen in only one direction or place, but in any
direction or place wherever the devotee casts his glance.
This knowledge is at once illuminational, direct, im-
mediate, homogeneous, and having no other condition
or object on which it is dependent. It is bereft of any desire.
As such, one who meditates on the Name of God with un-
swerving devotion and attention and supports it by scrip-
tural reading and intellectual study can also be said to pos-
sess this direct knowledge.        When the meditation is car-
ried on with faith and love, regularly, daily and for a long
time,   there    will   remain   no    desire   except   the   desire
to meet God; and the Name will be uttered not only by the
tongue, but also in the throat or in the mind.           These two
ways    of uttering the     name      are   respectively known as
Madhyama and Pasyanti. Beyond this lies also the fourth
way of meditation, namely, that which is done in the re-
gion of the navel without any effort or fear. Instead of
                         CHAPTER III

      SRI AMBURAO MAHARAJA OF INCHGIRI


                         Section A: Life


    Sri Amburao was born in 1857 in a small village of
Jigjivani in the Indi Taluka of the district Vijapur, in a
poor Brahmin family of a Kulkarni, by name, Srinivasarao.
As his uncle, Bapurao, was residing at Nimbargi, a village
six miles away from Jigjivani in order to serve his spiri-
tual teacher, Sri    Narayanarao       Maharaja,     Amburao     or
‘Baba’ as we shall call him hereafter,         was sent there to
have his primary education.        Naturally, Baba had several
occasions to meet the saintof Nimbargi, and we note that
this must have been the earliest but one of the most power-
ful influences which moulded his future spiritual life. Baba
had not even crossed his teenage when after finishing his
primary education he returned to Jigjivani perhaps only.
                                                      to
face adversities.   His parents died, and there followed in
1876-77 a great famine, causing innumerable deaths in the
country   on   account    of    starvation.   His   elder   brother,
Gopalarao could not make the two ends meet, and so Baba
left his home with his younger brother, Krshna, in order
to fitid food and shelter. After wandering on foot for many
days and for abottt लाह hundred and twentyfive miles he
happetied to reach Sankeshwara in the District of Belgaum.
On his way, there were occasions when Baba had to satisfy
his hutiger by eating the leaves of the tamarind tree. At
Sankeshwara, in the Math of Sri Sankaracarya, he served
as the drawer of water, and his brother used to clean the
utensils and sweep the         precincts of the Math. Baba was
so honest and lovable by nature that even while doing the
menial service, he could win the affection and regard of his
master.

    Famine over, Baba returned to Jigjivani and took the
position of a supervisor of the labourers in the construction
