  Secrion C;         DISTINCTION WITHOUT DIFFERENCE

       Did
         Ranade   differ irom   his   spiritual teacher
Bhausahib Maharaja, and his spiritual brother, Amburao
Maharaja in his method of imparting the Name 0 God”
Apparently, yes,       essentially, not. We do not know what
actually Bhausahib used to do but what Baba (Amburao)
used to do was to ask the would be disciple to place the
book    ‘Dasabodha’     on   his   head and   take the    oath   that
he would remain throughout his life free from the possi-
ble guilt of coveting the wealth and the women belonging
to others,    Baba would then put a pinch of             the   sacred
ashes    (Angara) in the mouth of the disciple and impart
to him the divine Name which he, on every such occasion,
used to hear directly from God or read it as being dis-
played before him in clear and distinct alphaket.              In no
case, the Name was arbitrarily chosen by Baba out of the
innumerable divine names written in the religious books,
probably with the firm belief that all such names are as
dead and useless as the parchment on which they are
written. Such names do not sprout in the immaculate
visions of God and so are said to be without the living
seed    (Nirbija).    On the coritrary, the Name that comes
directly from God and is therefore heard or seen and read
by the Guru (spiritual teacher) is said to be fully inform-
ed with the living spirit of God and is therefore capable of
giving rise to the various visions of God, provided how-
ever, it is meditated upon by the disciple regularly,
punctually and for fixed periods for a very very long
time.   This Name, in other words, is said to te “Sabija
that is with to be fully informed the living seed which would
sprout in the direct visiotis of God. Excepting the placing
                  The Summit at Nimbal                                919


of the ‘Dasabodha’ on head and the taking of oath, this
was exactly the method of initiation used by Ranade.

   Ranade    omitted    the    ritualistic     part of the act         of
initiation, namely, the placing of the ‘Dasabodha’ on head,
the taking of the oath and the eating of             the     ashes,     as
being of no vital importance, but retained the residual
portion of the act of initiation, namely, the imparting of
the divine   Name.     Here    too,   Ranade     had    his    distinct
rational mode of imparting the Name.            Not that he heard
or read the Name on every occasion              of    initiating      the
seekers; he only used to select the Name out of the several
Names which he had already heard or seen written dur-
ing his meditation and contemplation on the divine Name
and Forms of God,      The selection of        a particular Name
was also not arbitrary, nor was it imposed on a seeker
against his liking,   The     seeker was first       consulted;        he
was required to say to which          particular     deity     he     felt
devotion, or which name he liked most.               And      then on
knowing the particular deity or the particular name from
the seeker, Ranade used to impart that very name to the
Seeker and ask him to meditate on it.          In essence this was
no change in the method of initiation adopted by Baba
and Bhausahib,   For whereas the latter two used to know

what particular name was to be given to                a_ particular
person, Ranade had only to      take out that Name from his
stock of many such divine Names which he had already
heard or seen,   It is immaterial       whether the Name               is
Seen or heard as the occasion         arisesor whether it              is
chosen out of a number of names which have already
been seen or heard,    For the value of all these names is
eternally the Same; it does neither increase
                                             nor decrease
with the lapse of tim
                      e,


    We may say that Ranade had one additional advan-
tage, in that he had not to wait for the Name to be heard
or Seen, It was there already at hand. He had simply to
turn to it and use it, In this connection, we have to
narrate an interesting incident,
                                      Baba once      asked    a seeker
220     Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage

to    go to   him for being    initiated    the   next morning.       As
directed the person went to Baba; but as it ig human to
forget, Baba forgot the Name              which he had heard the
previous day.      Apologetically, therefore, he said           to    the
seeker, “Yesterday I     heard      the    Name    which     was to be
imparted to you and so I asked. you to come today; but
IT am not sure whether the Name I wish to impart to you
is the same as I heard yesterday. It is not in my power
to tell you the Name, as I like; so please come tomorrow.”
In the méantime Baba heard the same Name again and
he then imparted it to the sadhaka (seeker).


      From all this, one need not however come to the con-
clusion that Baba or Bhausahib             had no stock of Names
which they might have already heard                or seen     written.
Perhaps they intended         to   have a double        assurarice that
the Name to be imparted is chosen by God and                    not by
them,    But this is not an important point, for it makes
no difference in the capacity of a seed            10   grow, if it    is
tested Ohce or twice.     A seed which is good is gocd                for
ever and it mattets little whether it is brought freshlv
from the market or was there already in stock.


      No doubt, the Name acts like a seed.          But there is this
difference between the two.         The seed of corn is broken
and destroyed before it sprouts into a plant and a tree; the
divine name ever retains its soundness and ireshness, and
does not decay even if it is meditated upon by several
persons and in different times. Let ages pass without
having used it at any time, but it does not 1056 its power
of growing into divine experiences, if it is used again
and over again, It may disappear or may be forgotten,
just ag the immaculate forms of God or the unstruck
sounds and melodies cease to be heard for the time being,
but the divine Name is never destroyed              in its    potency.
Just as the sounds are revived by radio-activity but not
destroyed, even 50 power ‘of the Name to revive, visual or
auditory experiencés is néver destroyed; it depends on
the power of the Guru or what {s the same thing as the
                     The Summit at Nimbal                         221

    grace of God,   Meditation    makes   it   manifest.   Once     a
    certain teacher, Mr. Barve by name, went to Prof. Ranade
    and requésted him to initiate     him again a second time,
    as he had   forgotten   the   Name    imparted to      him    by
    Amburao   Maharaja,     Ranade    asked    him to go over to
    Inchgiri and stay there for three days and meditate either
    in the shrine of Baba or in that of Shri Bhausahib. The
    teacher did as he was told and to his surprise, the same
    Name which he had forgotten        came    into   his memory.
    Thus it is that the revival of the Name was the result of
    nothing else but the grace of God,


       Ranade did make one noteworthy change in the man-
    ner in which the Name was usually        imparted by
    Bhausahib and Baba, They did not depute their authority
    to initiate to someone else, but Ranade did so on almost
    all the occasions excepting a few when he himself initia-
    ted the seekers directly. He, however, did so because he
    had the authority of the saint of Nimbargi in this respect.
`   When Bhausahib was to be initiated, Nimbargi Maharaja
    got him initiated by his disciple Raghunathapriya, who
    was a Brahmin by caste and not like him a non-brahmin
    (ie, a Lingayata), In those days it was not customary for
    a non-brahmin to have a Brahmin like Bhausahib as his
    disciple. Of course, the important point to remember here
    is that for Bhausahib, not Raghunathapriya but Nimbargi

    Maharaja was the Guru for the Name which was imparted
    to Bhausahib    had   come from    Nimbargi       Maharaja.    It
    makes little difference if the seed is sown by the owner
    or by someone else under the orders of the owner so far
    as the crop is concerned, The seed will necessarily grow
    into a plant and a tree. Even so, Ranade thought that it
    would make little difference if the Name he wished to im-
    art was actually imparted by him or by someone else carry-

    ing out his order. Two advanced and elderly sadhakas.
    Kakasahib Tulpule and Kakasahib Karkhanis were
                                                    given
    this duty of initiating the aspirants as directed by the
      Tofessor, They did not ask the seeker to take an oath
    Tegarding the two negative moral virtues of keeping
222     Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage

himself away from coveting another               man’s    wealth and
land and from casting          a justtul glance on any woman,
They also gave other instruction regarding how and when
to meditate and do all other accessory spiritual activities,
Thus did Ranade bring about a change‘in
                                    the very proce:
dure of initiating the seekers of spivitual-lite, without in
any way diminishing the spiritual importance,


      Tnis might create a desire in the minas of some to
111118८6   some   one   else   py   imparting   unto   him     che   same

Name ot God with which he has been graced by his spi-
tuai teacher, and thereby biing           him into       whe    spiritual
fold.   But however laudable          this idea may be irom the
view-point of an   altruistic generous man, it is hignly
defective from the spiritual point of view.. No doubt, the
beed must fructity; the divine Name will yield a bumper
crop of spiritual experiences for the new man.                 But was
there any sanction for the man who transferred the Name
10 some one else ?        In the absence of sanction from the
Guru or from God it is a great blunder and an offence
against the Guru and God.            For ultimately, the sanction
must come from God, either in the form of a direct order’
or in the form of hearing new divine Names as the result
of intense and long meditation, and of the grace of God.
To accept and perform the role of the Guru is a hazardous
or rather a dangerous task; for it involves, as Professor
Ranade held, the acceptance on his own head the burden
of all the sins committed by the disciple and the respon-
sibility of warding of all his miseries, difficulties, poverty
and dangers in life. Besides, the Guru must know in
advance whether there is in ihe person who seeks the
Spiritual life at 1645६ the potential capacity for cultivating
the moral virtues and of maintaining the spiritual disc’-
pline neéded for a growing and healthy spiritual life, He
must have, in other words, a penetrating insight to dis-
cover if the soul of the seeker is a fertile ground where
the seed of the divine Name will easily take its roots, or
whether it is a hard rock where nothing can be sown and
nothing can be grown, Like all great seers Ranade used
                     The Summit at Nimbal                        293


  to know this as soon as he looked at any person, and ask
  him to-come next year, or say with delight that a parti-
  cular disciple was dong very fine. On one occasion, the
  moment he saw the widowed old sister of a student dis-
 ciple of his he exclaimed with great joy, “O, what a great
  lady!     If I am not to initiate her, whom should I    initiate
  then ?”


      A caution must be exercised by all spiritual teachers.
 For, certain so-called spiritual teachers     prefix    or     affix
 certain words to the      traditionally known divine Names
  (such as Rama and Krsna)       or a mantra    (sacred hymn)
 like the Gayatri mantra of a Brahmin, and suppose that
  the Name or the mantra is not only revived but has be-
 come powerful on account of the prefixes or the affixes.
 But this is a clear self-deception, and a deception worked
 on the disciples.    Even the time-old one-syllabled mantra,
 namely the Om, cannot       be said to be    genuine unless it
 comes out of the mouth of a person who has realized God
 and has the      power to show Him     to others.   Otherwise,
 neither will it be able     to work by itself, nor      when it
 added on to some other word or words as a prefix or
 affix,


    Regarding the days on which the Name used to be
 imparted, they were the same with all the three saints.
 Monday, Thursday and Saturday were these days. It was
 more or less a matter       of Convenience    rather    than     of
 auspiciousness which some credulous persons attach to
 only certain days of the week, and not to other days.
 Perhaps, the motive might have been to make a thorou
                                                      gh
 inquiry about the seekers of spiritual life, and to          ascer-
  tain and.understand the will of God during the inter-
  vening days, Perhaps it may be to prevent people from
  being impatient and to make them more serious to get the
  initiation, With Baba and Bhausahib, the place of initia-
ˆ tion was not necessarily Inchgiri or Umadi.        They used
  to go from place to place to meet their disciples and
                                                              spend
  three, five   or seven days, according to convenience,          in
224     Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage

doing    spiritual   activities of meditation,          Bhajana,      reading
of    spiritual]   literature    and     discussions       and   comments
Naturally, they did not insist upon the seekers to go to
Inchagiri or Umadi for having the initiation, though they
wele most welcome to visit these places whenever there
was a Spiritual gathering, for instance, on the anniversary
day of the passing away of their Guru or throughout the
month of Sravana for the purpose of meditation.                       On the
other hand, excepting one or two occasions, when Ranade
is reported to       have initiated      the seekers in       places    other
than     Nimbal, he never failed to tell them to come                        to
Nimbal for being initiated.             The purpose seems to be to
test the sincerity and the preparedness of the seekers to
undertake the journey as well as to find out in the mean-
time their capacity and worth to receive and nourish the
Spiritual life.    Indeed there were not a few who, notwith-
standing     their    knowledge         regarding Ranade’s           spiritual
height and the great value of               spiritual      instruction, did
not stir an, inch from the place where they lived nor made
up their mind to go to Nimbal. They wasted their life in
enjoying the pleasures of life,            and    therefore postponing
their visit to Nimbal.          It is   much     to   be    pitied    that   a
student of Professor Ranade would not or rather could not
go over to Nimbal even when he was living not beyond
twenty to fifty miles from Nimbal.               One such student who
belonged to Bijapur and moved up                      and down. several
times to Poona and Bombay, never cared throughout the
life of Ranade to stop at Nimbal, but as he himself reported
afterwards he was awakened in a dream                        and initiated
when Ranade had left the mortal coil! Another had the
uncotiscious pride that he had thé knowledge of a philoso-
pher and so considered himself to be too rational to allow
himself to go by the samé old credulous path of the
unthinking believers. “Are you greater than Kant who
discarded reason in order to make room for faith?’, a
friend of his asked him one day. Then, as a result of this,
he got himself intiated at Jamkhandi when Prof. Ranade
had gone there a year or so before his death! Ranade
knew the hearts of the péoplé and so he insisted upofi the

he liked one or the other name or to utter both the names
one after the other.            Being confused and bewildered by
the remarks of an ill-tutored person, the disciple, notwith-

the uttering of the Name loudly by him had altogether
destroyed the efficacy of that Name.                     The disciple had no
courage to approach Baba a second time, nor did he think

it Wise to disturb             Baba   in     his   great    illness     and   ask
whether        the   elderly    disciple     of    his     was    cofrect     andi
whether the loud utterance of the Name had completely

smile, “There was nothing               wrong       in     telling    Baba the
Name you had received from him loudly in his ears, as
he is your Guru, and as the Name is eternally immortal
it    cannot    at   all   decrease     in    power, even         if you pro-
nounce it loudly with all your might from the housetops.
You ought ta have appreciated the rational faith of Baba.”
(3) A third instance, if needed, is that of the reply which
Ranade     gave when            the   same disciple        narrated to        him

that the hymn addressed to the deity “Vyankatesh” was
recited by him during day-time and not at the dead of
night as Ought to have been according to what is written
in that hymn, and that therefore he need not hope to see
the face of God. “You are a student of philosophy, and
how is it that you entertain such a doubt? Is there for
God any distinction between day and night?                            The fruit
of devotion, and not of mechanical recitation, must always
be the same, whether the devotional act happens by day
or by night.”


       From this one can easily understand why in Profes-
501    Ranade’s       mind      there      must     not    have      been     any
difference in the ways in which the Name is uttered,
whether by means of tongue as the saint Tulsidasa has
                           ६
                  The Summit at Nimbal                               227


 recommended us to do or to         utter    the Name mentally
 along with the ingoing and outgoing breath as the saint
 Kabira has commanded us to do. Those who have closely
 ooserved him meditating     will    testify to       ihe    fact that
 Ranade used both the methods as they suited him.                   Nay,
 sometimes,   he used to   meditate    on      the   Name      in    the
 throat, or sing it melodiously and loudly.          And it will not
 be too much to    surmise   that    occasionally      he    used     to
 meditate so silently on the Name of God, that the con-
 Sciousness of the ingoing   and the outgoing           breaths also
 was an hindrance to him.     Some would like to call this
 state of his mind as that of ‘Sahaja kumbhaka’,                where
 there occurred the   automatic suspension of breath.               But
 to say so is also not correct, for even this state of ‘Sahaja
 kumbhaka’ wouid last only for a            short    time.   Ranade’s
 meditation   was not conditioned even by            this stat2.     His
 Main and the only business was the devotional uttering
 of the Name.   It had no connection in the least with the
 continuation or the Suspension of breath.           The Name used
 to Spring up within him from the region of his navel, and
 he was content to be consciously aware of it. It was a
 trance in which the mind uttered the Name and the mind
 heard it as it was being uttered so much so that uttering
 Was not different from hearing; nor were the two pro-
 cesses of hearing and uttering dissociated from the visual
 process of gazing at the immaculate Form of God, as well
 as from listening to the various unstruck sounds,              When
~ added on to this there mingled in his meditation several
 other factors namely the non-sensuous, tactual, olfactory,

 gustatory experiences and the experiences of horripilation,
 lightness of body, shedding of the tears of joy and grati-
 tude, the choking of the    throat, who        can say      that his
 meditation of the divine Name did not include in it the

  bliss of being one with God? Was it simply the yogic
 Samadhi during which the energy in the spinal cord rose

 fo the roof of the brain for the time being, or the supra-
228     Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


mental consciousness during         which    the   supreme spirit
alone was reigning from top to toe ?


      This will further explain how the division he makes
in his ‘Mysticism in Maharashtra’ of mystics into Rational,
Devotional, Activistic and Practical, is not at all a water-
tight   division but that how a mystic          according to his
innate disposition and temperament differs           from    others
in the emphasis he lays upon the rational, devotional
activistic and practical aspects of mysticism, how in fact
the mystical aspect of a saintly character lies at the back
of his devotion, intellect, activity        and worldly wisdom.
One has to understand in other words, that a mystie of
a very high order like “Jnanadeva, Tukarama or Ramadass
possesses necessarily all ihe -above-mentioned           qualities,
simply because they. are all God-realized perfect saints.
Exactly in this strain, Ranade has said in his ‘Mysticism
in Kannada        Literature’ that a saint is either Tyagi or
Bhogi, Rogi or Yogi, meaning thereby that he has either
renounced the pleasures of life or welcomes.them with
joy, or that he was more or less always suffering from
some kind of illness or perpetually tuned with the Infinite.
One is tempted to say that this is perhaps an autobic-
graphical touch in his writings. Ranade himself was.
 throughout his life, from 1909 to 1957, ill on account of 8
dangerous disease; like Aristotle or Yajnavalkya he was
 not against enjoying the pleasures of life; yet from the
 bottom of His heart, he had given up all sorts of attach-
 ment not ofily for the pleasures of life but also for all
 God-less and perishable objects of the world. And all
 this was quite easily possible for him because             he   was
highly strung in constant unison with God. 1 was of
 account    of   his   God-intoxicated,   suprasensuous,     supra:
 mental and supra-intellectual condition of joyful conscious
 ness that he could rise above all the duals of life. How
 else are we to explain that he could do most efficiently
 all the duties of the Head of the Departmerit of Philo-
                    The Summit at Nimbal                              229


 sophy or the duties of the Dean or of the Vice-chancellor,
‘and’ carry on at the same time his meditational activities
 for hours at a stretch on the meagre diet of a few ounces
 of liquid food and a small piece of bread? Like Jesus
Christ, he has shown to the world that a man does not
live by bread alone,                           -


    Look     to   his   ingenuous     method     of satisfying        the
craving Of the senses.      It was in March or April 1927 that
he told a student living in his house : ‘Leave off your even-
ing meals, if possible,’ and then not long afterwards, told
him not to starve his       senses.   Then he       explained        away
the contradiction by saying: ‘If you should desire to eat
sweetmeat, put a small piece of it on your tongue                     and
throw it out”      How beautifully indeed has he combined
tyaga with bhoga, renunciation with the pleasures? This
he recommended especially to a sick soul, and enjoined
upon him regular meditation on the Name of God.

     Professor Ranade did not and could not move from
Place to     place, visit   his   disciples     and revitalise       their
Spiritual    activities   by doing       with     them    meditation,
Bhajans,     reading of spiritual literature        and     explaining
its meaning, along with discussions and their own com-
ments. Possibly, Ranade did not wish to do so for two
 reasons,    One reason was       that   he was      totally     against
“creasing his own fame as against that of his Guru,                   even

 though it might be incidental and without any motivation
 Another. reason seems to be more, plausible.               He       might
have thought that the very excellent points of spiritual
 importance that might -have emerged during                    the    dis-
 cussions,   explanations and     comments of Guru        might       have

 become the exclusive possession of some of his disciples
 क 4 particular place, but’denied to             other    disciples     at
 other places, In order to remove this incidental drawback
 Ranade must have preferred the coming together of the
 maximum number of the disciples and seekers of spiritual

 life from the maximum number of places at Nimbal after
230      Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


the schools       and the      colleges      were closed about the mid-
-dle of April every year.- “Why do you come
                                            late in the
 last week of May-and not earlier? You could have
                                                   met
So    and   so,   and      conversed    with      them.   That        would    have
been     of advantage         to all.” This        is what       Ranade wrote
and    spoke      to   a   student of       his   who     was    a     disciple   cf
Amburao Maharaja.


      This however does not mean that Ranade thought that
each and        every person who came to Nimbal deserved                          to
know all that happened there.                     He did make discrimina-
tion between man and man                     and in their            capacities   to
understand.        Besides, he        was    careful not        to    divulge the
secrets of others which were confided to him with great
trust,      A   student      of his    was very      fortunate         in    having
prompt replies to his letters from Professor Ranade.                              On
One occasion, he did not get the reply for one month and
a half; then suddently afterwards he read in a letter from
Ranade:         “That was one of the best letters you have ever
written to me during the last 25 years.” The student had
narrated a dream of his in which he had touched the feet
of Ranade shedding tears of gratitude on them.                              But the
wonderful thing about the dream was that even after the
dream was over, and the student was fully awake tears
were flowing down his cheeks. Ranade did not wish others
should know about this; and so though every time once
                        his scores of letters in some
in a week he was disposing
way or other, he did neither destroy that letter nor filed
it nor replied it, but used to tell Dadasahib Deshpande
to keep it buried in a niche in the wall where it was.
People around him were curious to know the contents of
all the letters when they were filed, replied or destroyed;
but nobody showed any interest in reading that letter of
the student which was allowed simply to take rest in the
niche. Thus it was that Ranade kept the contents of that
letter a guarded secret from all other people

      When on another occasion, the same student happen-
ed to put his step into the room in which Ranade was
                      The Summit at Nimbal                                231

talking with some other people at Nimbal, Ranade looked
at him and said with joy “Oh, what a fine health?” The
student      understood       what     Ranade      meant;       but     others
incjuding even Mr. G. V. Tulpule, could not understand
Ranade, because there was               nothing      wrong       with     that
student at any time before he came to Nimbal. Some one
of them said, “Why, he has been all the time in excellent
health.” Ranade simply said to them in reply,                      “He    has
understood, what I meant.” After we all left the room
everyone asked the student, ‘What did you understand ?
We have not been able to make out what Ranade said to
you.” The Student 100 was 101 a dullard. He said, “Why
should I lose the compliment when Ranade told you that
I had understood him?”            What indeed Ranade meant was
that the student had meditated well throughout the pre-
vious year; but as it was not meant for                 all, he spoke in
a language which should be               understood         only by       that
student,


    Again in 1954, a very remarkable incident happened
With reference to that same student.                 Ranade asked         him
if he could recollect two occasions, one at Sangli in 1923
and another at Allahabad in 1928, when he did something
which was unique and extraordinarily meritorious. ‘Yes,’
Said the student, and          he     showed    to    Professor        Ranade
what he meant by the signs of his                    hand      only.    “Quite
right,” said the Professor, This time, however, the student
was not harassed by others,


    How fortunate it was for this very student that after
everyone had departed            from the hall at Nimbal, Ranade
used    to   Stand   in   a   small   room   and     calling    the    student
allow him to touch his feet!            A repetition of this happen-
ed once      in the palace of the Rajasahib              of Sangli.       The
student took the permission of Professor Ranade at about
4 p.m. to leave Sangli. The usual custom since the time
of Nimbargi Maharaja was that no person was permitted
to approach the saint a second time after he was permit-
ted,
   to leave the place and this was continued in Ranade’s
232    Prof. ह. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


time   2150.   Notwithstanding    this    practice,    the   student
who had to wait somehow in the palace for
                                          two or three
hours more thought of seeing Professor             Ranade      again.
Ranade then was meditating in another              building       at    a
distance of about 200 yards. After finishing his medita-
tion he was Coming from that building to the place where
he was putting up with Dadasahib Deshpande.              None was
on the road which was lit by the moon.           The student who
was Waiting for the opportunity went forward with con-
fidence and joy and strange to say, Ranade said, “You
wish to bow down ?” Saying so he removed his shoes, and
gladly allowed the student to touch his feet. Similarly on
another   occasion,   in   Delhi when everyone        of about         150
people had left the hall of the          late   Balwantrao        Datar
(Minister of State for Home) and when Ranade too had
gone about fifty feet along the long corridor leading 10
his room, he suddenly turned back and calling the student
by the sign of his hand said to him, “You have brought
the Attara; apply it soon to my hand.”            We    must       only
imagine the kind of joy and satisfaction the student must
have felt.     All these instances, are sufficient to point out
that Ranade behaved with persons as they deserved.


    Shri Narayanrao Maharaja, the saint cf Nimbargi -s
reported to have told Amburao to close his eyes, ears and
mouth and silently meditate upon the name of God. This
teaching of the saint amounts to what the Bhagavad Gita
has said regarding the       nature of Brahmayoga,           namely,
“He whose mind is not attached to the external contacts
(of objects, but) obtains the bliss in the Atman, is one
whose mind is attached to Brahma-yoga, and who experi-
ences imperishable bliss.” (B.G. 5.21) His disciple Shri
Bhausahib Maharaja did not say so in so many words but
behaved in the same manner especially during meditation
in standing posture from 12 to 2 at night. This illustrates
what Nimbargi Maharaja had told Amburao. Amburao
Maharaja no doubt acted upon the advice of Shri Nimbargi
Maharaja but we think that he went a step further be-
cause he considered himself as a corpse devcid               of    any
                The Summit at Nimbal                       233


sensuous knowledge, during meditation on the name           of
God. Professor Ranade like his Guru Shri Bhausahib
Maharaja did not say any thing regarding the closing of
the eyes, ears and mouth.   In fact he very often used to
keep his eyes and ears wide open while meditating, but
excepting the form   which he used to see and        the   un-
struck sound which he used to hear, he did not see any-
thing else or heard anything else.   For all practical pur-
poses he was both blind and deaf; even     so   as   he    had
cultivated the habit of silent meditation on the name of
God, the’ question of opening his mouth never arose,
                         APPENDIX —1

      NOTE WORTHY FOLLOWERS OF THE SCHOOL


                     SHIVALINGAVVA


Shivalingavva :

      Shivalingavva of Jath was one of the greatest devo-
tees of Shri Bhausahib  Maharaja.  Even when she was
not yet of ten years old, she had received the spiritual
seed of divine name from Shri Bhausahib Maharaja. That

She was picked up by her Guru from a bevy of forlic-
some girls is not without significance.      She was so much
 enamoured of the meditative     life that she was not pre-
 pared even to get. herself married.    But on     the advice of
‘her Guru, she got herself married.     As nature would have
it,   a Son was also born to her who unfortunately died and
 her husband also died and though she was grieved, she
 could by the grace of her     Guru    turn her bereavement
 into meditative life.   She composed a poem in which she
 has described that a son has been born           to     her.   Fools
might say that it was an illegitimate child born to her,
but this is not so. It was the divine immortal child made
 of light, whom she could see always playing with                her.
 Tt is not given to any one to have this experience. It was
 the fruit of a long, long sincere devotion to God.             It is
 said that people saw her burning camphor on              her   very
palm for the purpose of waving light before her Guru.
She could meditate at a stretch for six hours, changing
her posture after the end of three hours. That she had
seen her own face and had had many photic, phonic and
morphic experiences as also visions of several by gone
 saints during her meditation is      also   a   fact.    All these
 were the fruits of her silent meditation on the Name of
 God.


      Once she had gone to    Pandharpur with her Guru.
 And as a miracle would have it, she saw as if in a vision
                             Appendix                                      235

that flowers were showered from above on the head of
the deity of Pandharpur and her Guru.                  We do not doubt
this incident because she had given an account of it in
a letter to Prof. Ranade.      She had no ambition of becom-
ing a Guru, though incidentally              a    few      persons        were
initiated by her into the spiritual life.               Professor R. D.
Ranade never bowed down before any person, but he did
so on the feet of this great Iady, and .so it appears that
when Ranade compares this lady with Mahadevi Akka or
with Muktabai it is not without any reason.


Narsappa Sapethi:

       There was at Bijapur        a mason       by    name       Narsappa
Sapethi,      After he had attained the age of 85 years and
When he became unable to do his work, he began to beg
for his livelihood, but never accepted more than a piece
of a bread and more than one quarter of an anna, and
when the collection became              rupees eleven       he    used       to
Spend    the   money in feeding         the poor      disciples   of      Shri
Nimbargi Maharaja,         Selfishness and greed never touched
this   man.    Several people have heard him, saying loudly :

‘Victory, Victory to the saint of Nimbargi and inscrutable
are    the   glory   and   power   of    Guru!’       He   used    to     visit
Nimbal and meet Professor Ranade                 while going         to    his
home. Once while he was at Nimbal he said to Professor
Ranade: ‘How wonderful is           this house        which you have
built for here in any part of it is              heard     the    unstruck
sound of the name of God.’         It appears that he was sitting
for meditation throughout the whole of the night for once
Professor Ranade said about him, when he was 105 years
old, to Mr. Jagannath Lele — ‘just see how this old man
is sitting and meditating even at the dead of the night.’


Shattyappa
         :

       Shattyappa was one of the most faithful servants of
Shri Bhausahib        Maharaja.    Once     he said to Maharaja:

‘Iam sorry, I cannot meditate for a long time. But I shail
do the work of looking after your horse very well.’ Upon
236     Prof. R. D. Ranade and. His Spiritual Lineage

‘this Bhausahib Maharaja asked him not to worry, but to
 keep the horse in good condition. ‘Do not worry, I shall
meditate for     you,’   added    Sri Maharaja.
                                          This continued
upto the end of the life of Shri Bhausahib Maharaja. But
afterwards Shattyappa began to meditate seriously and it
is said that he got into the habit of meditating for nine
hours,     Two remarkable things can be mentioned about
him,     One was that even though he was utterly illiterate,
he began to read Dasabodha and            Jnanesvari.   Professor
Ranade said about him that he must have been, in one
of his previous lives, one of the carriers of the palanquin
of Saint Jnanadeva,         Another instance about him is that
Professor Ranade’s sister Yamunakka began to become a
little kit intolerant about his meditation for long hours
and doing no domestic work at the house            of   Professor
Ranade,     It appears that Professor Ranade heard her say-
ing something against him, especially         about his   taking
meals and tea at his house without doing any work.           She
was told by Ranade that he will first give Shatlyappa
half of the piece of a bread which he would get and then
eat the remaining half since he was doing the highest
kind of duty, namely, allegiance to God. It was indeed
a great fortune of Shattyappa that he was loved by Professor
Ranade.

Sri Ramchandrarao Yaryyatikar: Chimad:

Shri Bhaurao Kaka of Savalsang:
    He was a well-built and tall person and the fingers
of his hand touched his knees, even while he was stand-
ing. He had a melodious voice and used to sing very
loudly in the temple of Bhimrao at Nimbargi.              His voice
was so loud that what he used to sing was clearly heard
in the village of Nimbargi at a distance of two furlongs.
He had full faith in his Guru and had attained the gieatest
heights in Paramartha.    He died in Tikota near Bijapur
and his samadhi is also there.


Shri Dajiba Patil of Satalgaum:
    He was a resolute and           stubborn   disciple    cf    Shri
Nimbargi Maharaja.      Once he     was   present in a     room at
the top of the entrance door of the temple and attending
the spiritual sermon of his Guru. In the course of his
teaching the Saint happened to say, ‘If one wculd medi-
tate with faith and devotion on         the name    of God,       He
Would protect him in every way. ‘If that is so, let us,
you and I sit together in this very room and see if God
cares or gives us our mid-day food,’ said 1221108.        Nimbarg
Maharaja tried his best to impress upon him that they
Should not test God in that manner, but that was all in
vain, Thereupon the saint said, ‘Well if you so wish, let
Us sit for meditation in this very room and see what God
does for us.’ Accordingly both of them sat for meditation.
When one hour was over, Dajiba asked the saint, “Why
does your God not give         us    anything to eat.”          ‘Have
patience and’continue your meditation,’ replied the saint.
Two or three hours passed and yet there was none.
Dajiba became thoroughly impatient Lut could not leave
the Place bécause Nimbargi Maharaja was there. In the
238   710. ह. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


meantime,      some    rich   men     from    Kolhapur came        ६0
Nimbargi in order to pay a visit to the saint.            They went
to the house of the saint, but were informed that Maharaja
was Still in the temple.       So they returned to the temple
and went to the       room where Maharaja          was sitting and
placed     before   Nimbargi     Maharaja      the    sweet-meats,
mangoes and other sweet things which they had brought
as present,    Nimbargi Maharaja said to them, “Please do
not keep them all before 706.          Give them all to Dajiba
who is sitting there.’ Thus was Dajiba convinced of the
truth of the teaching, he had heard from the saint in the
morning.


Girmalappa :                                          |
    Girmalappa was born in 1873. He was a resident and
a celebrated merchant of Jamkhandi. He had strengthen-
ed his body by physical exercises and games.              Being very
Yich and    generous by disposition, he built a temple at
Inchgiri   as also built a spacious audience hall between
the temple of his       Guru    and    that   of   Shri    Nimbargi
Maharaja in order to perpétuate the memory of his Guru
Shri Bhausahib Maharaja. And the most noteworthy point
to be remembered in this connection is that                he   never
allowed anybody to know of it. His disgust for all God-
less things increased along with the increase in his spiri-
tual experiences atid all this can be illustrated by his .not
being daunted on account of the great financial loss that
he suffered in hig business. He was not only a builder
of the temple of stones, but he had also saved many a
soul by imparting spiritual knowledge io them for about
16 years and died at Inchgiri in the year 1934. One very
important aspect of his life was that he was so humble
that om one occasion when he wished to visit Shri
Amburao Maharaja, he approached him not by walking
the distance but by prostratitig on the road for about a
quarter of a furlong. This shows that his regard for Shri
Amburao Maharaja was as great as his regard was for
his Guru Shri Bhausahib

Lingappa "5000107 :
   Lingappa Savalgi was a student in the Agriculture
Department of the Deccan college when Professor R. D.
Ranade was also there before joining the Fergusson College
Lingappa was Such a veteran sadhaka that he used to
keep awake for hours together during nights and do his
meditation even in day time, whenever he was free from
his studies. His method of meditation was unique. In his
room he used to keep a table in the middle of the four
walls and would sit upon it for meditation so that if sleep
overtook him, he should fall on the ground.          He had no
compromising attitude so far as his meditation was con-
cerned.   He used to board the train at Hutagi at about 8
in the night and reach Poona at about 11 in the morning
next day.   And the wonderful thing about him was that
he used to sit for meditation at Hutagi and get up from
meditation at Poona. He never cared to hear music of
the singers or the songs as recorded in the gramophone

plate for he used to hear the melodious unstruck sound.

          MISTRY TURNED INTO HAPPINESS

Pleased with me and Jook at me with great affection, or
become displeased and get away without sipping a spoon-
ful of the excellent tea he would prepare, Even ten or
 twelve times during 24 hours, I had to do this drill, and
each time was a time of joy to me.                His displeasure or
anger too lasted only for a few seconds and so I used
to like his being angry with me for I was sure it was
 affection and love in disguise.
      Seeing that his whole day passed in reading, dictating
 to his steno, attending the university duties and medita-
 tion on the bank of the river Yamuna, I first thought he
 Would enjoy Sound sleep by night. But hardly did he
Sleep for a couple of hours for I was sleeping just outside
 his room in the hall, He did not sleep, and I could not.
 For I can now say that it was a great privilege and a
 great pleasure of my life that I could not but enjoy the
250        Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


Sweet and the melodious tunes in which he was singing
the divine         Name ‘Narayana’.          It is   no        exaggeration         to
say    that     while      hearing    him      singing,         I   felt     I    was
myself singing the Name.               One day while preparing his
tea at dead of night he said to me, “I am                             glad       your
‘Sravanabhakti’, devotion by way of hearing  the Name
being sung by another, is going on very well. I did not
then       understand the       exact meaning of
                                         that ‘Sravana-
bhakti’, and now there is none to sing that way-neither
myself nor         even the best singer of the country.                     Indeed,
who could have slept, except a dead stone, while he was
Singing the Name? That is why whenever he called me
at any time during nights, I did not require to be called
a SeCond time,            ‘Yes sir, I am,’ was always my response.
Being pleased with me possibly he said to me one day,
“You        have    conquered     your   sleep.”          And       today,       after
a lapse of fifty four years, 1 have lost this all.                         Neither
ean    I    have    the    ‘Sravana-bhakti’,        nor       the   condition      of
having conquered the sleep.              I     do     remember             that    he
suggested me         a remedy to keep myself awake by night.
“Leave off your evening              meals”, but          he added         on     the
words, ‘if possible. “Nights are long enough if one wants
to meéditate,” he           told me in plain words. Along with
this, he told me to sit for meditation for three hours at a
stretch, from 3 a.m. to 6 am. not minding even if the
legs were to break.           Accordingly even after his death, he
appeared to me in my dreams three or four iimes, saying
“Vinayak, get up, it is three o’clock, sit for meditation.”
Just at that very moment, I used to hear three strokes of
the bell in the nearby police station at Jodhpur. I now
repent -for all my foolishness and obstinacy because 1
have not left my evening meals, nor tried even for two
or three successive days to meditate from 3 to 6 before
sunrise, How can my devotion grow from ‘Sravana to
Manana (silent meditation) and how can I understand
that-Manana is at once both ‘Sravana and utterance of
the Name of God”? I am however certain  of one thing,
that Guru’s grace is on me, |                             -

           ‘Let me go back        and    complete      the   narration           of ‘my
     struggle in   life    only   with    the   view    of   impressing           upon

     the minds of readers as to how the grace of God can work
     out miracles,   It was in 1920 that I was waiting for the
     result of my .Matriculation Examination.                 But instead of
     sitting idle, I accepted my first service of Rupee one per
_    day in a furniture shop belonging to one Mr. Patange, in
     the    Main   street    of    the    cantonment         of        Poona.      This
     Mr, Patange,     who is now reported to be a millionaire,
     started his shop at. the advice of my uncle, who had be-
     come a sannyasin.       I served in the shop for 8 days; then
     with the help of a section officer in the sixth Division
    ` ण   the Military Department Poona I got a job of a clerk
     on Rs, 40/- per month.         On the 18th of May, 1920 I passed
    -my Matriculation Examination               and my salaray               rose    to
     Rs, 60/- p.m. from that very day. But I made up my mind
     to leave the job and join the Willingdon college at Sangli.
     My sannyasi uncle was totally against my joining the
     college, He advised me not to give up the job. He was
     correct in a way for had I not resigned I would have
     earned a salary Rs. 2000/- p.m, and drawn a nice pension, us
     it happened     in    the    case   of one   of my colleagues, Not
      minding the displeasure of my uncle I went to Jamkhandi

      aid of 85. eight only from Mr. Bhausahib Kale, as well
      as Some extra-money to start my college career in Sangli.

      number of marks in Logic.             My    Principal            G.   C.   Bhate
      became muth pleased with me, and used to help me by
      Jending any book I wanted to read. He was my Professor
    , Of Philosophy also and he wished very much to have me
     -9 the staff of the Willingdon college in 1933 after I was
     Telieved from my job of Assistant Professor of English
     -and Philosophy at the Rajarama College, Kolhapur.

           It is however interesting to know how I was appointed
    at Kolhapur,          After my       two-years’ -job          at    Poona      was
      Over in 1928 I went to Bombay and stayed at my father-

in-law’s    house with the intention        of writing           a thesis in

one anna for tram and three quarters of an anna for tea
and bread.     Prof. N. A. Thooti, Reader in Sociology used
to,
  be kind to me.            He once   told me,        “You       should   be

to God, It was Dr, Thooti who said in the Academic
Council of the Bombay University, “Mr. Date should be
allowed to submit his thesis for M.A. in Sociology, even
though he has stated in his application that he is working
 under     Professor    R.    D.   Ranade   of   the        University    of

of our University, the Votes counted and not the head.
 I got a letter from the university informing me that my
 request could not be granted. Then              it   was        as I   have
already narrated I went over to Allahabad, worked for
 one month and a half and appeared the same year th
 1929 with 8:papers in philosophy and got the degree of
 M.A, in high 2nd class from the University of Bombay.
 All this was nothing but the grace of God, which came
 upon me through Professor Ranade.


      For about two months and a half from June 1930, 1
 worked as a teacher in the Gokhale Education Society’s
 High School in Bombay. One day in reply to my applica-
‘tion I’got a letter from the University of Allahabad that
 a ‘Research scholarship might be available for two years
  in the Department of Philosophy, I jumped with delight
- at the idea that I would get an opportunity to work under
‘Professor Ranade. So, I resigned my job in Bombay and
 went straight to. Allahabad. As Professor Ranade was
                           Appendix                         953


` never assertive so far as the secular affairs were concern-
  ed, the Research Scholarship was divided between one
  Mr, 0. उ. L. Kapoor and me. Even then, I thought the
  opportunity to work under Ranade ought not to be lost.
  I accepted to have half the scholarship of Rs. 50/-, one
  fourth of Which was to be depcsited in the University
  according to the then existing rules and this amount was
  to be given to me at the end of two years and after the
  submission of the thesis for Research. Prof Ranade wished
  me to stay at his residence, but I told him that as I was
  to get the scholarship and as I was with my wife it would
  be more in the fitness of things if I stayed in Daraganj.
  He accepted my request and allowed me to stay separately.
  Yet, whenever he wished, both of us used to go immedi-
  ately to his place and stay there upto a week or so. Once
  on the day of Dassera, it so happened that we were about
  to put a morse] in our mouth of the sweets my wife had
  prepared on that so-called auspicious day, we hardly knew
  that a 77०6 auspicious event was to take place that very
  moment.      Mahavir, the driver of the car of Ranade came
  up and told us that “Sahib is waiting for you to go with
  him to his residence.”    We left our dinner, gave all the
  sweets etc.   to our neighbour and   took our seats in    the
  car, Ranade was promptiy careful to ask me to sit by his
  Side and my Wife to have her seat beyond me.         I   could
  understand his motive and let me hope the readers too
  will understand what Ranade had in his mind.       His heart
  was always on his palm, it was so transparent and guile-
  less that he spoke nothing but truth. He liked the bread
  Prepared by my wife, because it was baked in the manner
  in which he wished it 10 be baked, So he told his wife,
  a Vinayak’s wife bake the bread so long ६४ she is here.’
      ow far the truth was digested by his wife, I do net know.


  ५       Regarding my restarch work, I wished to write upon
  “Three Master-minds in the New Testament.” My motive
  in choosing the subject cannot be said to be without any
  bias for I started with a prejudiced mind.       Throughout
      a
254   Prof. R. D. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


my college career and before and after it, I found that
Christian writers would somehow bring in the Christian
viewpoint that Jesus alone is the saviour of mankind and
dub with discredit all the Hindu saints and the Hindu
religion.For very good reasons, I never appreciated this
missionary zeal in propagating the Christian ideal of
saintliness,I was a student of philosophy and as I had
taken lessons in philosophy from Professor Ranade, I had
no grudge in accepting whatever was rational and reason-
able as truth.      But what I found was that even text book
writers     of philosophy, Metaphysics,     Ethics    and   Religion
were partial to the Christian faith.        In order to counter-
balance     this   one-sidedess   and exuberance of zeal in one
direction, I wished 10 examine the very foundations of
such a wrong edifice.       I worked in the University Library
for a fortnight in preparing a Bibliography on the sub-
ject of my thesis.      I was struck with surprise that it was
an ocean of literature.      And during the next two or three
months, as my reading of the Bible and of relevant books
increased, the place of my prepossession             and prejudice
was taken by        admiration and adoration for Jesus, John
and Paul, and I began to think that none of them was
less of a Saint than any Indian saint,        But I found that
the literature was so vast that it would have been impos-
sible for me to wade through it during the two years at
my disposal, I therefore approached Professor Ranade
and ‘requested him to allow me to modify my thesis and
keep its title as “Philosophy of St. Paul.” I was submit-
ting my articles every two or three months and Professor
Ranade was much pleased to see my progress. But after
the lapse of one year, I again requested him to allow me
to curtail the scope of my thesis to “Some problems in
the philosophy of St, Paul.” Even though my thesis was
good, fortunately it was not published in the annals of the
University, For, I am now free to publish my two books
which I am preparing, namely, ‘The Beautiful and the
sublime in the Old Testament,” and “Master-minds in the
New Testament — Jesus, John, Peter and Paul.”

        That very afternoon,     afier   dinner at Dr. Bapat’s a

future time, you shall have to pay my travelling expenses
in case you call me for an interview.” Now, I know that
what I did was against my own interest. But 7 still
 remember that while writing and posting the application

                      APPENDIX — 3


       | SOME OUTSTANDING MIRACLES AS ARE
                   KNOWN TO DR. DATE


    Who is not tempted and influenced by the occurrence
of a miracle ? Ordinary people generally call it a sign
of spiritual life, and so a: measure of the spiritual worth
of aman. The capacity to work out a miracle ‘is sufficient
to endow upon him knighiship or the title of ‘Mahatma’.
Apart however from this general belief, it must be clearly
borne in Mind that miracles are not manufactured by the
saints; they. occur because the saint lives the life of devo-
tion to God_and to his Guru. Really, speaking a miracle
                            Appendix                                265

ean be said to be a sign of the power and grace of God,
which manifest to protect his devotee by remcving his
difficullies and     dangers.   At   the   same time,     a miracle
ought to be considered as a sufficient guarantee that God
who is Mercy incarnate will never desert his devotees,               It
ought to increase his faith, his devotion and his feeling
of dependence on the wisdom and the saving power cf
God,   Many a time, a miracle it is which              moulds       the
character of a man by bringing about a sudden change in
his life.   He then becomes a ‘new’ personality altogether.
A confirmed sinner may become a great saint, a persecu-
tor of the saints may become their protector.


     Looked at from this point of view, I can              say    with
confidence    that   miracles   have   nol    only    increased     my
faith and devotion for God, but that they have also shown
me that God is my ultimate shelter and protector. Keep-
ing this in mind, I shall mention here some of the note-
worthy miracles which had occurred either in my life or
are known to me,


1.   The first and the foremost miracle is that I who could
have been at the best no better than a hotel-boy or a fourth
Class servant in some office in a deserted village, or a
drawer of water or a cook, had it not been for my good
fortune of coming in contact with one of the greatest of the
saints the world has ever produced and consequently raised
10 the status of a Professor in a university, and ranked as a
scholar of no mean repute.


2.   That I could have in Mrs. Malatibai a contented wife,
friend and counse] who has been with me through thick
and thin for the last fifty six years.        I   think   that it    4s
Only due to the grace of God that my two 5:75, who might
have been employed in a grocer’s आणू could have                   had
their highest possible education and are earning a lot in
the United States      of   America.   That    they    are perfectly
clean in their habits and conduct, that they have main-
266     Prof. R. 7. Ranade and His Spiritual Lineage


tained an unimpeachable and spotless            characier and are
above all, devoted to God and’ to Guru and are affectio-
nate and obedient to their parents is certainly miraculous
in the    present   times   of assertiveness   and   self-sufficiency
in a country like the U.S.A.        The eldest son, Vishvanath
is M.R.C.P. of. London, and the next to him Raghunath is
2 Ph.D.  in. Chemical Engineering.   That our two highly
educated daughters, Kamal and Vimal are behaving as
faithful and loving wives and mothers and are as equally
devoted as our sons, is also a sign of the grace of God.


3. It was at Bagalkot in January, 1925 that I spent a
few days at Deputy Collector, D. D. Deshpande’s house
Incidentally, Ranade came there during my stay to meet
Mr,   Deshpande,    for what purpose I do not know.            That
very night and in the next morning I was suffering from
pain due to the stiffening of my back.         I was even unable
to breathe properly. But when Ranade returned with
Mr, Deshpande from a visit to some one in the city, I
kept a smiling face in order that he should not know that
I was suffering     from an ache in the         back.   But    after
getting down from the tonga, he asked even while he was
away from me ata distance of fifteen to twenty yards
if I was suffering from ache in the kack. And after coming
inside he himself applied some iodine


4.    Professor Ranade wrote to me in reply to my letter
that I should be able to get through the M.A. Examination
in 2nd class with eight papers, even if the time was only
fortyfive days.     Relying on his    words     I    went over   to
Allahabad, stayed in his house and prepared myself for
the examination of 1929 of the University of Bombay
Some of my friends there laughed at my credulous nature
and asked me that if I was so sure of coming in 2nd class
why should I not give them sweetmeats in advance
Immediately I gave them a grand treat at Allahabad and
then came to Bombay to take the examination. To the
great surprise of my friends in three or four papers I had
                         Appendix                                    267

got first class marks,    Professor Ranade’s           words        came
true,


5. I was in Amalner, during 1929-30 as a fellow of the
Institute of Phiiosophy. One evening my wife Malatibai
had lighted a lamp as usual before our family deities.
While tuning away from the lamp her sari caught fire.
That very moment I came with a bucket full of water
which I had drawn from the nearby well, I saw the
dangerous situation of my wife        who was trying to extin-
guish the fire by pressing the sari on the ground. Aghast
with fear, my trembling hand put the bucket on the
threshold of the kitchen, and lo!       the flow of water that
came with force did the work of extinguishing the fire.
I did not remember the name of God at that time, nor
was there   a moment’s time to pray to God or the Guru.
Similar must have been the staie of mind of my wife too.
But why was she saved?         Possibly it was, one might say,
an ordinary instance of chance, possibly a result of the
unseen   meritorious   acts,   possibly   again       because       God
Wished   that She should increase her      faith       and     do    her
meditation with greater devotion and        regard.         To us    the
last alternative seems to be more probable than others,
and we believe that this miracle had happened for increas-
ing our regard and faith in God.                  ~    ~



6. It was in 1936 or 19357 I suppose that just when I was
at the main gate of his residence at Nimbal, Professor
called me and said loudly ‘Come on, Doctor’.               I went near
him and after touching his feet said, ‘Now that you have
called me ‘Doctor’, I think I am to get the degree of Ph.D’
A few years after that my friend and colleague Professor
M. A. Karandikar, of the Lingraj College, Belgaum got
his doctorate of the University of Bombay.                 Soon after-
‘wards Karandikar said    to    me    that I too would get the

to me that exactly after       four   months   I submitted my

                foreword to the book, Professor Ranade

7.    In 1938, I fought an election for a seat on the Senate
of Bombay     University   against   Prof. 8. V. Dandekar of
Poona.    It was a neck to neck fight, and while the count-
ing of votes was going on I was sitting in nearby garden
behind the University and was watching with great joy
the vision of God which covered        the     sea from        Marine
Lines to the Malabar Hill.     While     I    was     thus     deeply
engrossed, my friend Mr. B. V. Joshi brought the news of

Ranade came to know of my defeat, he wrote to me that
even without election, I would be, on many university-
bodies like Academic council, senate and Faculty of Arts.
This came out literally true afterwards.

8.    Twice did I dream, just five minutes before I woke

me in the dream, “Vinayak, you have to go to the Bank

you have to go to the bank today.’ When I said with
surprise, “you have told me this very thing to do in my
dream just five minutes ago,” he simply smiled and said.
‘Yes, it Sometimes happens like that.’

daily before going to bed juice of ripe tomatoes mixed
with honey. I wrote to him about the dream. In reply,
he advised me to do as I was told in the dream.

the screw out by forcing water into her nostrils.             But as

great Satisfaction. But where must have the screw gone?
I then suggested to have one more’ X-ray photograph of
her stomach and thank God, it was seen as being lodged
in her lower intestines. The next morning it came out
along with the stools. It ought to be clear that my heart-
felt prayer was heard by God and my daughter was saved

17. It was in 1950 that early in the morning one day, I

though the     tangible     effect of that grace           was    seen only

act of his sending the angara to me.

the Gaekwara police station, and informed that police

20. Every one of my four children—two sons and two
daughters — had agreed to sing one devotional song every-
day and they had the sanction of Shri Gurudeva to do
so. My daughter Kamal used to sing the song, ‘Vithala,
Vithala Gajari etc.” This was immensely liked by
Ranade. One day in the year 1953 while we were in
